      <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Universe" title="Marvel Universe">
       Marvel Universe
      </a>
      , publishers have been able to introduce different variations of Spider-Man outside of mainstream comics as well as reimagined stories in many other
      <a href="/wiki/Multiverse_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Multiverse (Marvel Comics)">
       multiversed
      </a>
      spinoffs such as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Spider-Man" title="Ultimate Spider-Man">
        Ultimate Spider-Man
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2099" title="Spider-Man 2099">
        Spider-Man 2099
       </a>
      </i>
      , and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man:_India" title="Spider-Man: India">
        Spider-Man: India
       </a>
      </i>
      . Marvel has also made its own parodies of Spider-Man in comics such as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Not_Brand_Echh" title="Not Brand Echh">
        Not Brand Echh
       </a>
      </i>
      , which was published in the late 1960s and featured such characters as Peter Pooper alias Spidey-Man,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and Peter Porker, the Spectacular
      <a href="/wiki/Spider-Ham" title="Spider-Ham">
       Spider-Ham
      </a>
      , who appeared in the 1980s. The fictional character has also inspired a number of deratives such as a
      <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man:_The_Manga" title="Spider-Man: The Manga">
       manga version of Spider-Man
      </a>
      drawn by
      <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
       Japanese
      </a>
      artist
      <a href="/wiki/Ryoichi_Ikegami" title="Ryoichi Ikegami">
       Ryoichi Ikegami
      </a>
      as well as
      <a href="/wiki/Hideshi_Hino" title="Hideshi Hino">
       Hideshi Hino
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       The Bug Boy
      </i>
      , which has been cited as inspired by Spider-Man.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Also the French comic
      <i>
       Tl-Junior
      </i>
      published strips based on popular TV series. In the late 1970s, the publisher also produced original Spider-Man adventures. Artists included Grald Forton, who later moved to America and worked for Marvel.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Supporting_characters">
       Supporting characters
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Spider-Man_supporting_characters" title="List of Spider-Man supporting characters">
       List of Spider-Man supporting characters
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Spider-Man has had a large range of
      <a href="/wiki/Supporting_character" title="Supporting character">
       supporting characters
      </a>
      introduced in the comics that are essential in the issues and storylines that star him. After
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_and_Mary_Parker" title="Richard and Mary Parker">
       his parents
      </a>
      died, Peter Parker was raised by his loving aunt,
      <a href="/wiki/Aunt_May" title="Aunt May">
       May Parker
      </a>
      , and his uncle and father figure,
      <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Ben" title="Uncle Ben">
       Ben Parker
      </a>
      . After Uncle Ben is murdered by a
      <a href="/wiki/Burglar_(comics)" title="Burglar (comics)">
       burglar
      </a>
      , Aunt May is virtually Peter's only family, and she and Peter are very close.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Debut_43-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Debut-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/J._Jonah_Jameson" title="J. Jonah Jameson">
       J. Jonah Jameson
      </a>
      is depicted as the publisher of the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Daily_Bugle" title="Daily Bugle">
        Daily Bugle
       </a>
      </i>
      and is Peter Parker's boss and as a harsh critic of Spider-Man, always saying negative things about the superhero in the newspaper. Despite his role as Jameson's publishing editor and confidant
      <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Robertson_(comics)" title="Robbie Robertson (comics)">
       Robbie Robertson
      </a>
      is always depicted as a supporter of both Peter Parker and Spider-Man.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saffel21_45-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-saffel21-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Flash_Thompson" title="Flash Thompson">
       Eugene "Flash" Thompson
      </a>
      is commonly depicted as Parker's high school tormentor and
      <a href="/wiki/Bullying" title="Bullying">
       bully
      </a>
      , but in later comic issues he becomes a friend to Peter.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saffel21_45-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-saffel21-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Meanwhile
      <a href="/wiki/Harry_Osborn" title="Harry Osborn">
       Harry Osborn
      </a>
      , son of Norman Osborn, is most commonly recognized as Peter's best friend but has also been depicted sometimes as his rival in the comics.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gcd_47-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-gcd-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Peter Parker's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romantic_interest" title="Romantic interest">
       romantic interests
      </a>
      range between his first crush, the fellow high-school student
      <a href="/wiki/Liz_Allan" title="Liz Allan">
       Liz Allan
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saffel21_45-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-saffel21-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      to having his first date with
      <a href="/wiki/Betty_Brant" title="Betty Brant">
       Betty Brant
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-origins_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-origins-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the secretary to the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Daily_Bugle" title="Daily Bugle">
        Daily Bugle
       </a>
      </i>
      newspaper publisher J. Jonah Jameson. After his breakup with Betty Brant, Parker eventually falls in love with his college girlfriend
      <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stacy" title="Gwen Stacy">
       Gwen Stacy
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gcd_47-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-gcd-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mnyc_50-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-mnyc-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      daughter of
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Police_Department" title="New York City Police Department">
       New York City Police Department
      </a>
      detective captain
      <a href="/wiki/George_Stacy" title="George Stacy">
       George Stacy
      </a>
      , both of whom are later killed by
      <a href="/wiki/Supervillain" title="Supervillain">
       supervillain
      </a>
      enemies of Spider-Man.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saffel60_55-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-saffel60-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saffel60_55-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-saffel60-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Mary_Jane_Watson" title="Mary Jane Watson">
       Mary Jane Watson
      </a>
      eventually became Peter's best friend and then his wife.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saffel124_67-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-saffel124-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Felicia Hardy, the
      <a href="/wiki/Black_Cat_(comics)" title="Black Cat (comics)">
       Black Cat
      </a>
      , is a reformed
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cat_burglar" title="Cat burglar">
       cat burglar
      </a>
      who had been Spider-Man's girlfriend and partner at one point.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sanderson83_62-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-sanderson83-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Enemies">
       Enemies
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Spider-Man_enemies" title="List of Spider-Man enemies">
       List of Spider-Man enemies
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Writers and artists over the years have established a
      <a href="/wiki/Rogues_gallery" title="Rogues gallery">
       rogues gallery
      </a>
      of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supervillains" title="Supervillains">
       supervillains
      </a>
      to face Spider-Man. In comics and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Spider-Man_enemies_in_other_media" title="List of Spider-Man enemies in other media">
       in other media
      </a>
      . As with the hero, the majority of the villains' powers originate with scientific accidents or the misuse of scientific technology, and many have animal-themed costumes or powers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        note 6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Examples are listed down below in the ordering of their original chronological appearance:
     </p>
     <p>
      <b>
       Note:
      </b>
      Alter ego characters who are the most high profile in the supervillain alias but others have shared that supervillain name are in bold.
     </p>
     <div class="legend">
      <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #b6fcb6; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
      </span>
      signifies a group team.
     </div>

          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vault68_135-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Vault68-135">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          129
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        <br/>
        John Romita Sr.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hobgoblin_1_134-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Hobgoblin_1-134">
          <span>
           [
          </span>

          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Back35_136-0">

          <span>

        </sup>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>

     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Archenemies">
       Archenemies
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Unlike a lot of well known rivalries in comics book depictions. Spider-Man is cited to have more than one archenemy and it can be debated or disputed as to which one is worse:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archenemy_144-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-archenemy-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ol>
      <li>
       <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1">
        <b>
         <a href="#ref_1">
          ^
         </a>
        </b>
       </span>
       Doctor Octopus is regarded as one of Spider-Man's worst enemies and archenemy. He has been cited as the man Peter might have become if he had not been raised with a sense of responsibility.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeFalco_10-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-DeFalco-10">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         10
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_145-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CNN-145">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         139
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       He is infamous for defeating him the first time in battle and for almost marrying Peter's
       <a href="/wiki/Aunt_May" title="Aunt May">
        Aunt May
       </a>
       . He is the core leader of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sinister_Six" title="Sinister Six">
        Sinister Six
       </a>
       and has also referred himself as the "Master Planner". ("
       <a href="/wiki/If_This_Be_My_Destiny...!" title="If This Be My Destiny...!">
        If This Be My Destiny...!
       </a>
       ")
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBR_.235_146-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CBR_.235-146">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         140
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Later depictions revealed him in Peter Parker's body where
       <a href="/wiki/The_Superior_Spider-Man" title="The Superior Spider-Man">
        he was the titular character for awhile
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_145-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CNN-145">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         139
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_2">
        <b>
         <a href="#ref_2">
          ^
         </a>
        </b>
       </span>
       Norman Osborn using the Green Goblin alias is also commonly described as Spider-Man's archenemy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
        <a href="#cite_note-147">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         141
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
        <a href="#cite_note-148">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         142
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archenemy_144-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-archenemy-144">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         138
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Mostly after he is responsible for setting up the death of
       <a href="/wiki/Gwen_Stacy" title="Gwen Stacy">
        Spider-Man's girlfriend
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/The_Night_Gwen_Stacy_Died" title="The Night Gwen Stacy Died">
        one of the most famous Spider-Man stories
       </a>
       of all time which helped end the
       <a href="/wiki/Silver_Age_of_Comic_Books" title="Silver Age of Comic Books">
        Silver Age of Comic Books
       </a>
       and begin the
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age_of_Comic_Books" title="Bronze Age of Comic Books">
        Bronze Age of Comic Books
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archenemy_144-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-archenemy-144">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         138
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       He was thought to be dead after that but writers help bring him back from the
       <a href="/wiki/1990s_in_comics" title="1990s in comics">
        1990s
       </a>
       and he returned to plaque Spider-Man once more in the comic books (such as being involved of the killing of
       <a href="/wiki/Aunt_May" title="Aunt May">
        Aunt May
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Dark_Reign_(comics)" title="Dark Reign (comics)">
        other heroes
       </a>
       (such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Avengers_(comics)" title="Avengers (comics)">
        Avengers
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25.5_149-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-25.5-149">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         143
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       ). He is also a enemy of Spider-Man sometimes just as Norman and not just only as the Green Goblin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN_.2313_150-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-IGN_.2313-150">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         144
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_3">
        <b>
         <a href="#ref_3">
          ^
         </a>
        </b>
       </span>
       Another character commonly described as archenemy is Venom. Eddie Brock as Venom is commonly described as the mirror version or the evil version of Spider-Man in many ways.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archenemy_144-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-archenemy-144">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         138
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newsarama_1_99-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Newsarama_1-99">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         93
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Venom2_137-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Venom2-137">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         131
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Venom's goals is usually depicted as trying to ruin Spider-Man's life and mess with Spider-Man's head when it comes to targeting enemies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Venom_139-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Venom-139">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         133
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       He is one of the few villains depicted as unbeatable to Spider-Man without a few weaknesses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
        <a href="#cite_note-151">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         145
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Venom is also one of the most popular Spider-Man villains.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
        <a href="#cite_note-152">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         146
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       This popularity has led him to be an established iconic chacter of his own with own
       <a href="/wiki/Venom_(comics)" title="Venom (comics)">
        comic book stories
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">
        <a href="#cite_note-153">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         147
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Venom2_137-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Venom2-137">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         131
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ol>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_influence">
       Cultural influence
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Comic book writer-editor and historian Paul Kupperberg, in
      <i>
       The Creation of Spider-Man
      </i>
      , calls the character's superpowers "nothing too original"; what was original was that outside his secret identity, he was a "nerdy high school student".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kupperberg_154-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Kupperberg-154">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        148
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       :5
      </sup>
      Going against typical superhero fare, Spider-Man included "heavy doses of soap-opera and elements of melodrama." Kupperberg feels that Lee and Ditko had created something new in the world of comics: "the flawed superhero with everyday problems." This idea spawned a "comics revolution."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kupperberg_154-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Kupperberg-154">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        148
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       :6
      </sup>
      The insecurity and anxieties in Marvel's early 1960s comic books such as
      <i>
       The Amazing Spider-Man
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       The Incredible Hulk
      </i>
      , and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/X-Men" title="X-Men">
        X-Men
       </a>
      </i>
      ushered in a new type of superhero, very different from the certain and all-powerful superheroes before them, and changed the public's perception of them.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
       <a href="#cite_note-155">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        149
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Spider-Man has become one of the most recognizable fictional characters in the world, and has been used to sell toys, games, cereal, candy, soap, and many other products.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knowles_156-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Knowles-156">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        150
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Spider-Man is well received as a comic book character, always appearing as one of the greatest comic book characters or
      <a href="/wiki/Superhero" title="Superhero">
       superhero
      </a>
      of all time and almost always being the top Marvel Comics character. Spider-Man was declared the number one superhero on
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bravo_(US_TV_channel)" title="Bravo (US TV channel)">
       Bravo
      </a>
      's Ultimate Super Heroes, Vixens, and Villains tv series in 2005.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
       <a href="#cite_note-157">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        151
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empire_(magazine)" title="Empire (magazine)">
        Empire
       </a>
      </i>
      magazine placed him as the fifth-greatest comic book character of all time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
       <a href="#cite_note-158">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        152
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Wizard_(magazine)" title="Wizard (magazine)">
        Wizard
       </a>
      </i>
      magazine placed Spider-Man as the third greatest comic book character on their website.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wizard_159-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Wizard-159">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        153
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">
       IGN
      </a>
      placed Spider-Man third on IGN's Top 100 Comic Book Heroes of All Time in 2011, being only behind
      <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">
       DC Comics
      </a>
      characters
      <a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">
       Superman
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">
       Batman
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
       <a href="#cite_note-160">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        154
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Spider-Man has become Marvel's flagship character, and has often been used as the company mascot. When Marvel became the first comic book company to be listed on the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">
       New York Stock Exchange
      </a>
      in 1991, the
      <i>
       Wall Street Journal
      </i>
      announced "Spider-Man is coming to
      <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">
       Wall Street
      </a>
      "; the event was in turn promoted with an actor in a Spider-Man costume accompanying Stan Lee to the Stock Exchange.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wright_4-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-Wright-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       :254
      </sup>
      Since 1962, hundreds of millions of comics featuring the character have been sold around the world.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
       <a href="#cite_note-161">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        155
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Spider-Man joined the
      <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s_Thanksgiving_Day_Parade" title="Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade">
       Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade
      </a>
      from 1987 to 1998 as one of the balloon floats,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APCBS_162-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-APCBS-162">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        156
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      designed by
      <a href="/wiki/John_Romita_Sr." title="John Romita Sr.">
       John Romita Sr.
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sketch45_163-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sketch45-163">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        157
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      one of the character's signature artists. A new, different Spider-Man balloon float is scheduled to appear from at least 2009 to 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-APCBS_162-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-APCBS-162">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        156
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1981, skyscraper-safety activist
      <a href="/wiki/Dan_Goodwin" title="Dan Goodwin">
       Dan Goodwin
      </a>
      , wearing a Spider-Man suit, scaled the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sears_Tower" title="Sears Tower">
       Sears Tower
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
       Chicago
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">
       Illinois
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Tower_(Dallas)" title="Renaissance Tower (Dallas)">
       Renaissance Tower
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">
       Dallas
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
       Texas
      </a>
      , and the
      <a href="/wiki/John_Hancock_Center" title="John Hancock Center">
       John Hancock Center
      </a>
      in Chicago, Illinois.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Skyscraper_Defense_164-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Skyscraper_Defense-164">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        158
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_with_Spider-Man.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2731" data-file-width="4096" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Barack_Obama_with_Spider-Man.jpg/220px-Barack_Obama_with_Spider-Man.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Barack_Obama_with_Spider-Man.jpg/330px-Barack_Obama_with_Spider-Man.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Barack_Obama_with_Spider-Man.jpg/440px-Barack_Obama_with_Spider-Man.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_with_Spider-Man.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        U.S. President Barack Obama pretending to be caught in Spider-Man's web
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      When Marvel wanted to issue a story dealing with the immediate aftermath of the
      <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">
       September 11 attacks
      </a>
      , the company chose the December 2001 issue of
      <i>
       The Amazing Spider-Man
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">
       <a href="#cite_note-165">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        159
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2006, Spider-Man garnered major media coverage with the revelation of the character's secret identity,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166">
       <a href="#cite_note-166">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        160
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      an event detailed in a full page story in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">
        New York Post
       </a>
      </i>
      before the issue containing the story was even released.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167">
       <a href="#cite_note-167">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        161
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2008, Marvel announced plans to release a series of educational comics the following year in partnership with the United Nations, depicting Spider-Man alongside
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Peacekeeping_Forces" title="UN Peacekeeping Forces">
       UN Peacekeeping Forces
      </a>
      to highlight UN peacekeeping missions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168">
       <a href="#cite_note-168">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        162
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" title="BusinessWeek">
        BusinessWeek
       </a>
      </i>
      article listed Spider-Man as one of the top ten most intelligent fictional characters in American comics.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">
       <a href="#cite_note-169">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        163
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Rapper
      <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">
       Eminem
      </a>
      has cited Spider-Man as one of his favorite comic book superheroes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">
       <a href="#cite_note-170">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        164
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">
       <a href="#cite_note-171">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        165
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2015, the
      <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">
       Supreme Court of the United States
      </a>
      decided
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Kimble_v._Marvel_Entertainment,_LLC" title="Kimble v. Marvel Entertainment, LLC">
        Kimble v. Marvel Entertainment, LLC
       </a>
      </i>
      , a case concerning royalties on a
      <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">
       patent
      </a>
      for an imitation web-shooter. The opinion for the Court, by Justice
      <a href="/wiki/Elena_Kagan" title="Elena Kagan">
       Elena Kagan
      </a>
      , included several Spider-Man references, concluding with the statement that "with great power there must also comegreat responsibility".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">
       <a href="#cite_note-172">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        166
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">
       Awards
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      From the character's inception, Spider-Man stories have won numerous awards, including:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Alley_Award#1962" title="Alley Award">
        1962
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Alley_Award" title="Alley Award">
        Alley Award
       </a>
       : Best Short Story"Origin of Spider-Man" by Stan Lee and Steve Ditko,
       <i>
        Amazing Fantasy
       </i>
       #15
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Alley_Award#1963" title="Alley Award">
        1963
       </a>
       Alley Award: Best Comic: Adventure Hero title
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
      </li>
      <li>
       1963 Alley Award: Top HeroSpider-Man
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Alley_Award#1964" title="Alley Award">
        1964
       </a>
       Alley Award: Best Adventure Hero Comic Book
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
      </li>
      <li>
       1964 Alley Award: Best Giant Comic -
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man Annual
       </i>
       #1
      </li>
      <li>
       1964 Alley Award: Best HeroSpider-Man
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Alley_Award#1965" title="Alley Award">
        1965
       </a>
       Alley Award: Best Adventure Hero Comic Book
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
      </li>
      <li>
       1965 Alley Award: Best HeroSpider-Man
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Alley_Award#1966" title="Alley Award">
        1966
       </a>
       Alley Award: Best Comic Magazine: Adventure Book with the Main Character in the Title
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
      </li>
      <li>
       1966 Alley Award: Best Full-Length Story - "How Green was My Goblin", by Stan Lee &amp; John Romita, Sr.,
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
       #39
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Alley_Award#1967" title="Alley Award">
        1967
       </a>
       Alley Award: Best Comic Magazine: Adventure Book with the Main Character in the Title
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
      </li>
      <li>
       1967 Alley Award Popularity Poll: Best Costumed or Powered HeroSpider-Man
      </li>
      <li>
       1967 Alley Award Popularity Poll: Best Male Normal Supporting Character
       <a href="/wiki/J._Jonah_Jameson" title="J. Jonah Jameson">
        J. Jonah Jameson
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
      </li>
      <li>
       1967 Alley Award Popularity Poll: Best Female Normal Supporting Character
       <a href="/wiki/Mary_Jane_Watson" title="Mary Jane Watson">
        Mary Jane Watson
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Alley_Award#1968" title="Alley Award">
        1968
       </a>
       Alley Award Popularity Poll: Best Adventure Hero Strip
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
      </li>
      <li>
       1968 Alley Award Popularity Poll: Best Supporting Character - J. Jonah Jameson,
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Alley_Award#1969" title="Alley Award">
        1969
       </a>
       Alley Award Popularity Poll: Best Adventure Hero Strip
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
      </li>
      <li>
       1997
       <a href="/wiki/Eisner_Award" title="Eisner Award">
        Eisner Award
       </a>
       : Best Artist/Penciller/Inker or Penciller/Inker Team1997 Al Williamson, Best Inker:
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Untold_Tales_of_Spider-Man" title="Untold Tales of Spider-Man">
         Untold Tales of Spider-Man
        </a>
       </i>
       #17-18
      </li>
      <li>
       2002 Eisner Award: Best Serialized Story
       <i>
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </i>
       vol. 2, #3035: "Coming Home", by
       <a href="/wiki/J._Michael_Straczynski" title="J. Michael Straczynski">
        J. Michael Straczynski
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Romita,_Jr." title="John Romita, Jr.">
        John Romita, Jr.
       </a>
       , and Scott Hanna
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="In_other_media">
       In other media
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:119px;max-width:119px">
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:117px;max-width:117px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tobey_Maguire_2007_Shankbone.jpg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="543" data-file-width="434" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Tobey_Maguire_2007_Shankbone.jpg/115px-Tobey_Maguire_2007_Shankbone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Tobey_Maguire_2007_Shankbone.jpg/173px-Tobey_Maguire_2007_Shankbone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Tobey_Maguire_2007_Shankbone.jpg/230px-Tobey_Maguire_2007_Shankbone.jpg 2x" width="115"/>
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:117px;max-width:117px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andrew_Garfield_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="3048" data-file-width="2526" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Andrew_Garfield_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/115px-Andrew_Garfield_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Andrew_Garfield_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/173px-Andrew_Garfield_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Andrew_Garfield_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/230px-Andrew_Garfield_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 2x" width="115"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         <a href="/wiki/Tobey_Maguire" title="Tobey Maguire">
          Tobey Maguire
         </a>
         (top) and
         <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Garfield" title="Andrew Garfield">
          Andrew Garfield
         </a>
         (bottom) have both portrayed Spider-Man on
         <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_in_film" title="Spider-Man in film">
          film
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_in_other_media" title="Spider-Man in other media">
       Spider-Man in other media
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Spider-Man has appeared in comics, cartoons, films, video games, coloring books, novels, records, and children's books.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Knowles_156-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Knowles-156">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        150
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On television, he first starred in the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">
       ABC
      </a>
      animated series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_(1967_TV_series)" title="Spider-Man (1967 TV series)">
        Spider-Man
       </a>
      </i>
      (1967-1970)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">
       <a href="#cite_note-173">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        167
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">
       CBS
      </a>
      live-action series
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_(TV_series)" title="The Amazing Spider-Man (TV series)">
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </a>
      </i>
      (19781979), starring
      <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Hammond" title="Nicholas Hammond">
       Nicholas Hammond
      </a>
      . Other animated series featuring the superhero include the
      <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_syndication" title="Broadcast syndication">
       syndicated
      </a>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_(1981_TV_series)" title="Spider-Man (1981 TV series)">
        Spider-Man
       </a>
      </i>
      (19811982),
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_and_His_Amazing_Friends" title="Spider-Man and His Amazing Friends">
        Spider-Man and His Amazing Friends
       </a>
      </i>
      (19811983),
      <a href="/wiki/Fox_Kids" title="Fox Kids">
       Fox Kids
      </a>
      '
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_(1994_TV_series)" title="Spider-Man (1994 TV series)">
        Spider-Man
       </a>
      </i>
      (19941998),
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_Unlimited" title="Spider-Man Unlimited">
        Spider-Man Unlimited
       </a>
      </i>
      (19992000),
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man:_The_New_Animated_Series" title="Spider-Man: The New Animated Series">
        Spider-Man: The New Animated Series
       </a>
      </i>
      (2003), and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Spectacular_Spider-Man_(TV_series)" title="The Spectacular Spider-Man (TV series)">
        The Spectacular Spider-Man
       </a>
      </i>
      (20082009). A new animated series titled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Spider-Man_(TV_series)" title="Ultimate Spider-Man (TV series)">
        Ultimate Spider-Man
       </a>
      </i>
      , starring
      <a href="/wiki/Drake_Bell" title="Drake Bell">
       Drake Bell
      </a>
      , premiered on
      <a href="/wiki/Disney_XD" title="Disney XD">
       Disney XD
      </a>
      on April 1, 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174">
       <a href="#cite_note-174">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        168
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A
      <a href="/wiki/Tokusatsu" title="Tokusatsu">
       tokusatsu
      </a>
      series featuring Spider-Man was produced by
      <a href="/wiki/Toei_Company" title="Toei Company">
       Toei
      </a>
      and aired in Japan. It is commonly referred to by its Japanese pronunciation "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supaid%C4%81-Man" title="Supaid-Man">
       Supaid-Man
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175">
       <a href="#cite_note-175">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        169
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Spider-Man also appeared in other print forms besides the comics, including novels,
      <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_literature" title="Children's literature">
       children's books
      </a>
      , and the daily newspaper
      <a href="/wiki/Comic_strip" title="Comic strip">
       comic strip
      </a>
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_(comic_strip)" title="The Amazing Spider-Man (comic strip)">
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </a>
      </i>
      , which debuted in January 1977, with the earliest installments written by Stan Lee and drawn by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Romita,_Sr." title="John Romita, Sr.">
       John Romita, Sr.
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176">
       <a href="#cite_note-176">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        170
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Spider-Man has been adapted to other media including games, toys, collectibles, and miscellaneous memorabilia, and has appeared as the main character in numerous
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spider-Man_video_games" title="Spider-Man video games">
       computer and video games
      </a>
      on over 15 gaming platforms.
     </p>
     <p>
      Spider-Man was also featured in a
      <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_in_film" title="Spider-Man in film">
       trilogy of live-action films
      </a>
      directed by
      <a href="/wiki/Sam_Raimi" title="Sam Raimi">
       Sam Raimi
      </a>
      and starring
      <a href="/wiki/Tobey_Maguire" title="Tobey Maguire">
       Tobey Maguire
      </a>
      as the titular superhero. The first
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_(2002_film)" title="Spider-Man (2002 film)">
        Spider-Man
       </a>
      </i>
      film of the trilogy was released on May 3, 2002; its sequel,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2" title="Spider-Man 2">
        Spider-Man 2
       </a>
      </i>
      , was released on June 30, 2004 and the next sequel,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_3" title="Spider-Man 3">
        Spider-Man 3
       </a>
      </i>
      , was released on May 4, 2007. A third sequel was originally scheduled to be released in 2011, however
      <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">
       Sony
      </a>
      later decided to
      <a href="/wiki/Reboot_(fiction)" title="Reboot (fiction)">
       reboot
      </a>
      the franchise with a new director and cast. The reboot, titled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_(2012_film)" title="The Amazing Spider-Man (2012 film)">
        The Amazing Spider-Man
       </a>
      </i>
      , was released on July 3, 2012; directed by
      <a href="/wiki/Marc_Webb" title="Marc Webb">
       Marc Webb
      </a>
      and starring
      <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Garfield" title="Andrew Garfield">
       Andrew Garfield
      </a>
      as the new Spider-Man.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">
       <a href="#cite_note-177">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        171
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">
       <a href="#cite_note-178">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        172
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179">
       <a href="#cite_note-179">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        173
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180">
       <a href="#cite_note-180">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        174
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181">
       <a href="#cite_note-181">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        175
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A sequel titled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Amazing_Spider-Man_2" title="The Amazing Spider-Man 2">
        The Amazing Spider-Man 2
       </a>
      </i>
      was released on May 2, 2014.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182">
       <a href="#cite_note-182">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        176
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183">
       <a href="#cite_note-183">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        177
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Most recently, Sony and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disney" title="Disney">
       Disney
      </a>
      have made a deal for Spider-Man to appear in the
      <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Cinematic_Universe" title="Marvel Cinematic Universe">
       Marvel Cinematic Universe
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">
       <a href="#cite_note-184">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        178
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On June 23, 2015, Marvel, Walt Disney Studios, and Sony Pictures jointly announced
      <a href="/wiki/Tom_Holland_(actor)" title="Tom Holland (actor)">
       Tom Holland
      </a>
      would star as Spider-Man and
      <a href="/wiki/Jon_Watts" title="Jon Watts">
       Jon Watts
      </a>
      would direct.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarvelSonyJune23_185-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MarvelSonyJune23-185">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        179
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadway_musical" title="Broadway musical">
       Broadway musical
      </a>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man:_Turn_Off_the_Dark" title="Spider-Man: Turn Off the Dark">
        Spider-Man: Turn Off the Dark
       </a>
      </i>
      , began previews on November 14, 2010 at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foxwoods_Theatre" title="Foxwoods Theatre">
       Foxwoods Theatre
      </a>
      on
      <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">
       Broadway
      </a>
      , with the official opening night on June 14, 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lustig_186-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Lustig-186">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        180
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-playaug_187-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-playaug-187">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        181
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The music and lyrics were written by
      <a href="/wiki/Bono" title="Bono">
       Bono
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/The_Edge" title="The Edge">
       The Edge
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">
       rock
      </a>
      group
      <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">
       U2
      </a>
      , with a book by
      <a href="/wiki/Julie_Taymor" title="Julie Taymor">
       Julie Taymor
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Glen_Berger" title="Glen Berger">
       Glen Berger
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Aguirre-Sacasa" title="Roberto Aguirre-Sacasa">
       Roberto Aguirre-Sacasa
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188">
       <a href="#cite_note-188">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        182
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       Turn Off the Dark
      </i>
      is currently the most expensive musical in Broadway history, costing an estimated $70 million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-March_189-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-March-189">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        183
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In addition, the show's unusually high running costs are reported to be about $1.2 million per week.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190">
       <a href="#cite_note-190">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        184
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
       Notes
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
      <ol class="references">
       <li id="cite_note-11">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-11">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation book">
          <a href="/wiki/Stan_Lee" title="Stan Lee">
           Lee, Stan
          </a>
          ; Mair, George (2002).
          <i>
           Excelsior!: The Amazing Life of Stan Lee
          </i>
          . Fireside.
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-684-87305-2" title="Special:BookSources/0-684-87305-2">
           0-684-87305-2
          </a>
          .
          <q>
           He goes further in his biography, claiming that even while pitching the concept to publisher Martin Goodman, "I can't remember if that was literally true or not, but I thought it would lend a big color to my pitch."
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpider-Man&amp;rft.aulast=Lee%2C+Stan%3B+Mair%2C+George&amp;rft.au=Lee%2C+Stan%3B+Mair%2C+George&amp;rft.btitle=Excelsior%21%3A+The+Amazing+Life+of+Stan+Lee&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=0-684-87305-2&amp;rft.pub=Fireside&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-12">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-12">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Free_Press" title="Detroit Free Press">
           Detroit Free Press
          </a>
         </i>
         interview with Stan Lee, quoted in
         <i>
          The Steve Ditko Reader
         </i>
         by
         <a href="/wiki/Greg_Theakston" title="Greg Theakston">
          Greg Theakston
         </a>
         (Pure Imagination, Brooklyn, NY;
         <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1566850118">
          ISBN 1-56685-011-8
         </a>
         ), p. 12 (unnumbered). "He gave me 1,000 reasons why Spider-Man would never work. Nobody likes spiders; it sounds too much like Superman; and how could a teenager be a superhero? Then I told him I wanted the character to be a very human guy, someone who makes mistakes, who worries, who gets acne, has trouble with his girlfriend, things like that. [Goodman replied,] 'He's a hero! He's not an average man!' I said, 'No, we make him an average man who happens to have super powers, that's what will make him good.' He told me I was crazy".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-16">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-16">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation book">
          <a href="/wiki/Steve_Ditko" title="Steve Ditko">
           Ditko, Steve
          </a>
          (2000).
          <a href="/wiki/Roy_Thomas" title="Roy Thomas">
           Roy Thomas
          </a>
          , ed.
          <i>
           Alter Ego: The Comic Book Artist Collection
          </i>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/TwoMorrows_Publishing" title="TwoMorrows Publishing">
           TwoMorrows Publishing
          </a>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-893905-06-3" title="Special:BookSources/1-893905-06-3">
           1-893905-06-3
          </a>
          .
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpider-Man&amp;rft.au=Ditko%2C+Steve&amp;rft.aulast=Ditko%2C+Steve&amp;rft.btitle=Alter+Ego%3A+The+Comic+Book+Artist+Collection&amp;rft.date=2000&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=1-893905-06-3&amp;rft.pub=TwoMorrows+Publishing&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
         "'Stan said a new Marvel hero would be introduced in #15 [of what became titled
         <i>
          Amazing Fantasy
         </i>
         ]. He would be called Spider-Man. Jack would do the penciling and I was to ink the character.' At this point still, Stan said Spider-Man would be a teenager with a magic ring which could transform him into an adult heroSpider-Man. I said it sounded like the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fly_(Red_Circle_Comics)" title="Fly (Red Circle Comics)">
          Fly
         </a>
         , which Joe Simon had done for
         <a href="/wiki/Archie_Comics" title="Archie Comics">
          Archie Comics
         </a>
         . Stan called Jack about it but I don't know what was discussed. I never talked to Jack about Spider-Man... Later, at some point, I was given the job of drawing Spider-Man'".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-20">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-20">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Jack Kirby in "Shop Talk: Jack Kirby",
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Will_Eisner" title="Will Eisner">
           Will Eisner
          </a>
          's
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Spirit" title="The Spirit">
           Spirit
          </a>
          Magazine
         </i>
         #39 (February 1982): "Spider-Man was discussed between
         <a href="/wiki/Joe_Simon" title="Joe Simon">
          Joe Simon
         </a>
         and myself. It was the last thing Joe and I had discussed. We had a strip called 'The Silver Spider.' The Silver Spider was going into a magazine called
         <i>
          Black Magic.
         </i>
         <i>
          Black Magic
         </i>
         folded with
         <a href="/wiki/Crestwood_Publications" title="Crestwood Publications">
          Crestwood
         </a>
         (Simon &amp; Kirby's 1950s comics company) and we were left with the script. I believe I said this could become a thing called Spider-Man, see, a superhero character. I had a lot of faith in the superhero character that they could be brought back... and I said Spider-Man would be a fine character to start with. But Joe had already moved on. So the idea was already there when I talked to Stan".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-22">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-22">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Simon, Joe, with Jim Simon.
         <i>
          The Comic Book Makers
         </i>
         (Crestwood/II, 1990)
         <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1887591354">
          ISBN 1-887591-35-4
         </a>
         . "There were a few holes in Jack's never-dependable memory. For instance, there was no
         <i>
          Black Magic
         </i>
         involved at all. ... Jack brought in the Spider-Man logo that I had loaned to him before we changed the name to The Silver Spider. Kirby laid out the story to Lee about the kid who finds a ring in a spiderweb, gets his powers from the ring, and goes forth to fight crime armed with The Silver Spider's old web-spinning pistol. Stan Lee said, 'Perfect, just what I want.' After obtaining permission from publisher
         <a href="/wiki/Martin_Goodman_(publisher)" title="Martin Goodman (publisher)">
          Martin Goodman
         </a>
         , Lee told Kirby to pencil-up an origin story. Kirby... using parts of an old rejected superhero named Night Fighter... revamped the old Silver Spider script, including revisions suggested by Lee. But when Kirby showed Lee the sample pages, it was Lee's turn to gripe. He had been expecting a skinny young kid who is transformed into a skinny young kid with spider powers. Kirby had him turn into... Captain America with cobwebs. He turned Spider-Man over to Steve Ditko, who... ignored Kirby's pages, tossed the character's magic ring, web-pistol and goggles... and completely redesigned Spider-Man's costume and equipment. In this life, he became high-school student Peter Parker, who gets his spider powers after being bitten by a radioactive spider. ... Lastly, the Spider-Man logo was redone and a dashing hyphen added".
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-97">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-97">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation journal">
          Mondello, Salvatore (March 2004). "Spider-Man: Superhero in the Liberal Tradition".
          <i>
           The Journal of Popular Culture
          </i>
          <b>
           X
          </b>
          (1): 232238.
          <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">
           doi
          </a>
          :
          <a class="external text" href="//dx.doi.org/10.1111%2Fj.0022-3840.1976.1001_232.x" rel="nofollow">
           10.1111/j.0022-3840.1976.1001_232.x
          </a>
          .
          <q>
           ...a teenage superhero and middle-aged supervillainsan impressive rogues' gallery [that] includes such memorable knaves and grotesques as the Vulture...
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpider-Man&amp;rft.atitle=Spider-Man%3A+Superhero+in+the+Liberal+Tradition&amp;rft.aufirst=Salvatore&amp;rft.aulast=Mondello&amp;rft.au=Mondello%2C+Salvatore&amp;rft.date=March+2004&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1111%2Fj.0022-3840.1976.1001_232.x&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Journal+of+Popular+Culture&amp;rft.pages=232-238&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=X">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>
     </div>

          <sup>

            <b>

       <li id="cite_note-30">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-30">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation book">
          Manning, Matthew K.; Gilbert, Laura, ed. (2012). "1970s".
          <i>
           Spider-Man Chronicle Celebrating 50 Years of Web-Slinging
          </i>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/Dorling_Kindersley" title="Dorling Kindersley">
           Dorling Kindersley
          </a>
          . p.60.
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0756692360" title="Special:BookSources/978-0756692360">
           978-0756692360
          </a>
          .
          <q>
           Spider-Man was a proven hit, so Marvel decided to expand the wall-crawler's horizons with a new Spider-Man title...Its first issue featured Spidey teaming up with the Human Torch against the Sandman in a Christmas tale written by Roy Thomas with art by Ross Andru.
          </q>
         </span>

          <q>
           Spider-Man swung into the pages of an all-new ongoing series in this first issue by writer Louise Simonson and penciler Greg LaRocque.
          </q>
         </span>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpider-Man&amp;rft.atitle=1980s&amp;rft.aufirst=Matthew+K.&amp;rft.au=Gilbert%2C+Laura%2C+ed.&amp;rft.aulast=Manning&amp;rft.au=Manning%2C+Matthew+K.&amp;rft.btitle=Spider-Man+Chronicle+Celebrating+50+Years+of+Web-Slinging&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.isbn=978-0756692360&amp;rft.pages=147&amp;rft.pub=Dorling+Kindersley&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-33">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-33">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         <span class="citation book">
          Cowsill, Alan; Gilbert, Laura, ed. (2012). "1990s".
          <i>
           Spider-Man Chronicle Celebrating 50 Years of Web-Slinging
          </i>
          .
          <a href="/wiki/Dorling_Kindersley" title="Dorling Kindersley">
           Dorling Kindersley
          </a>
          . p.184.
          <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
           ISBN
          </a>
          <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0756692360" title="Special:BookSources/978-0756692360">
           978-0756692360
          </a>
          .
          <q>
           Todd McFarlane was at the top of his game as an artist, and with Marvel's release of this new Spidey series he also got the chance to take on the writing duties. The sales of this series were nothing short of phenomenal, with approx. 2.5 million copies eventually printing, including special bagged editions and a number of variant covers.
          </q>

        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

          <sup>
           <i>

             a
            </b>

            <b>
             b

          <sup>
           <i>
            <b>
             c
            </b>
           </i>

        <span class="reference-text">
         Saffel, p. 60
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-56">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-56">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Saffel, p. 65, states, "In the battle that followed atop the Brooklyn Bridge (or was it the George Washington Bridge?)...." On page 66, Saffel reprints the panel of
         <i>
          The Amazing Spider-Man
         </i>
         #121, page 18, in which Spider-Man exclaims, "The George Washington Bridge! It figures Osborn would pick something named after his favorite president. He's got the same sort of hangup for dollar bills!" Saffel states, "The span portrayed...is the GW's more famous cousin, the Brooklyn Bridge. ... To address the contradiction in future reprints of the tale, though, Spider-Man's dialogue was altered so that he's referring to the Brooklyn Bridge. But the original snafu remains as one of the more visible errors in the history of comics."
        </span>
       </li>
       <li id="cite_note-57">
        <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
         <b>
          <a href="#cite_ref-57">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        <span class="reference-text">
         Sanderson,
         <i>
          Marvel Universe
         </i>
         , p. 84, notes, "[W]hile the script described the site of Gwen's demise as the George Washington Bridge, the art depicted the Brooklyn Bridge, and there is still no agreement as to where it actually took place."
        </span>
       </li>

          <q>
           Writer Gerry Conway and artist Ross Andru introduced two major new characters to Spider-Man's world and the Marvel Universe in this self-contained issue. Not only would the vigilante known as the Punisher go on to be one of the most important and iconic Marvel creations of the 1970s, but his instigator, the Jackal, would become the next big threat in Spider-Man's life.
